Booth's Algorithm	O(n)	O(n)
Euclid's Algorithm	O(log n)	O(log n)
Karatsuba Algorithm	O(n log n)	O(n log n)
Longest Sequence of 1 after flipping a bit	O(n)	O(n)
Swap two nibbles in a byte	O(1)	O(1)
Block Swap Algorithm	O(n)	O(n)
Maximum product of sub array	O(n^2)	O(n)
Maximum sum of hour glass in matrix	O(n^3)	O(n^2)
Max Equlibrium Sum	O(n^2)	O(n^2)
Leaders in array	O(n)	O(n)
Majority element	O(n)	O(n)
Lexicographically first palindromic string	O(n)	O(n)
Natural Sort order	O(n log n)	O(n log n)
Quick, Selection Sort	O(n^2)	O(n^2)
Weightes substring	O(n)	O(n)
Move hyphen to beginning	O(n)	O(n)
Manacher's Algorithm	O(n)	O(n)

31/07/23, 08:56 - Somnath Reddy: The concurrent transaction given in the table can lead to several issues due to conflicts between the transactions. The issues are:

1. **Lost Update Problem:** This problem occurs when two transactions access the same data item, and one overwrites the changes made by the other. In this case, T3 and T4 both write to B and C, respectively, which can cause a lost update problem.

2. **Inconsistent Read Problem:** This problem occurs when a transaction reads a data item that is being modified by another transaction and obtains an inconsistent value. In this case, T5 reads C after T4 has modified it, which can cause an inconsistent read problem.

3. **Dirty Read Problem:** This problem occurs when a transaction reads a data item that has been modified by another transaction but has not yet been committed. In this case, T4 modifies C but has not yet committed, and T5 reads the modified value, which can cause a dirty read problem.

To overcome these problems, we can use different types of lock-based protocols:

1. **Shared/Exclusive (S/E) Locks:** In this protocol, each data item is associated with a lock that can be either shared or exclusive. A shared lock allows multiple transactions to read the data item but not modify it, while an exclusive lock allows a single transaction to both read and modify the data item.

To use S/E locks in this scenario, we can do the following:
- T1 and T2 both acquire shared locks on A and B before reading them.
- T3 acquires an exclusive lock on B before writing to it.
- T4 acquires an exclusive lock on both B and C before writing to them.
- T5 acquires a shared lock on C before reading it.

2. **Two-Phase Locking (2PL):** In this protocol, each transaction follows two phases - growing phase and shrinking phase. In the growing phase, a transaction acquires locks on all the data items it needs before performing any write operation. In the shrinking phase, a transaction releases all the locks it acquired during the growing phase.

To use 2PL in this scenario, we can do the following:
- T1 acquires a shared lock on A during the growing phase and releases it during the shrinking phase.
- T2 acquires a shared lock on B during the growing phase and releases it during the shrinking phase.
- T3 acquires an exclusive lock on B during the growing phase and releases it during the shrinking phase.
- T4 acquires exclusive locks on B and C during the growing phase and releases them during the shrinking phase.
- T5 acquires a shared lock on C during the growing phase and releases it during the shrinking phase.

3. **Timestamp Ordering Protocol:** In this protocol, each transaction is assigned a unique timestamp, and transactions are executed in timestamp order. A transaction with a higher timestamp cannot read or write data items that have been modified by a transaction with a lower timestamp.

To use timestamp ordering protocol in this scenario, we can do the following:
- Assign unique timestamps to each transaction (T1-T8) in increasing order.
- Transactions are executed in timestamp order: T1, T2, T3, T4, T5, T6, T7, T8.
- If a transaction tries to access a data item that has already been modified by another transaction with a lower timestamp, it is aborted and restarted with a new timestamp.

08/08/23, 06:57 - Somnath Reddy: *Project Type Courses* under Discipline/Open Electives category:
1) Simulation Project
2) Special Project
3) Reading Course
4) Product Development Project
5) Laboratory Project
6) Design Project
7) Technical Answers to Real Problems Project

*Guidelines for PJT course registration and evaluation process:*
1. Students are expected to form a team and identify a faculty guide from any School to initiate the
process.

2. Project Team should comprise a *minimum of two to a maximum of five students only* from any
B.Tech Programme of any School

3. Domain specific / Interdisciplinary / Multidisciplinary / Cross-disciplinary projects are encouraged.
Guide will finalize the tentative title / area of the work and the team of students to work on each
project. *Course Registration will be opened on VTOP Login for the faculty members (Guide)* on
21-08-2023. (Pre-any discussion between the guide and the student is essential)

4. *Students can work for one project type course at any point of time.*

5. *Course Registration will be done by the respective Guide only.* The Guide will fill in the necessary
data (Project title and the Registration Number of all the students, proposed to work on each of the
projects) on VTOP Faculty Login.

6. Subsequently the course will reflect on the list of registered courses for that particular semester on
VTOP Student Login. *This three credit course will not affect the upper limit of 27 credits* allowed
for a regular semester.

7. *Minimum duration of the project period is six months and the maximum duration is 12 months.*
Once the Project work is completed and a tangible outcome (Research / Review Paper published /
accepted in Scopus / WS, Journal / Conference Proceedings: Product Design / Patent Application)
is reached, the Guide will post the marks out of 100 for each student on VTOP and submit

8. *Absolute Grading System will be followed for the listed project type courses* as per VIT Grading
Policy

9. Even after 12 months, if the team fails to complete the project, then the course will be de-
registered for the students,

import java.util.*;

public class Main {

public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
String s = scanner.nextLine();
int n = s.length();
Set<Character> vowels = new HashSet<>(Arrays.asList('a', 'e', 'i', 'o', 'u'));
int[][] dp = new int[26][n + 1];

for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
for (int j = 0; j < 26; j++) {
if (!vowels.contains(s.charAt(i - 1))) {
dp[j][i] = dp[j][i - 1];
} else {
dp[j][i] = dp[j][i - 1] + 1;
}
}
}

int maxLen = 0;
for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) {
for (int j = 0; j < 26; j++) {
if (dp[j][i] % 2 == 0) {
maxLen = Math.max(maxLen, i);
}
}
}

System.out.println(maxLen);
}
}
25/11/23, 11:10 - Venkat Vit: Mod-3 lab-2 q-2
import java.util.Arrays;
import java.util.Scanner;

public class Main {

public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);

// Take input from the user
int[] numbers = new int[6];
for (int i = 0; i < 6; i++) {
numbers[i] = scanner.nextInt();
}

// Calculate and print the minimum and maximum values
calculateAndPrintMinMaxSum(numbers);
}

private static void calculateAndPrintMinMaxSum(int[] numbers) {
Arrays.sort(numbers);

long minSum = 0;
long maxSum = 0;

// Calculate minimum sum (sum of first four numbers)
for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
minSum += numbers[i];
}

// Calculate maximum sum (sum of last four numbers)
for (int i = 1; i < 5; i++) {
maxSum += numbers[i]+2;
}

// Print the results
System.out.println(minSum + " " + maxSum);
}
}

import java.util.Scanner;

public class Main {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
int n = scanner.nextInt();
int m = scanner.nextInt();

// Special cases
if (n == 1 || m == 1) {
System.out.println(1);    // Player 1 wins
return;
}

// Check if there is an even-height tower
boolean evenTowerFound = false;
for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
if (m % 2 == 0) {
evenTowerFound = true;
break;
}
}

// Determine the winner based on even-tower check
if (evenTowerFound) {
System.out.println(2);    // Player 2 wins
} else {
System.out.println(1);    // Player 1 wins
}
}
}
25/11/23, 11:10 - Venkat Vit: import java.util.*;
public class Main {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);

int rows = scanner.nextInt();
int cols = scanner.nextInt();
String targetWord = scanner.next();

// Check if the target word is empty
if (targetWord.isEmpty()) {
System.out.println("No");
return;
}

char[][] grid = new char[rows][cols];
for (int i = 0; i < rows; i++) {
String line = scanner.next();
for (int j = 0; j < cols; j++) {
grid[i][j] = line.charAt(j);
}
}

boolean found = searchWord(grid, targetWord);
if (found) {
System.out.println("Yes");
} else {
System.out.println("No");
}
}

private static boolean searchWord(char[][] grid, String targetWord) {
for (int i = 0; i < grid.length; i++) {
for (int j = 0; j < grid[0].length; j++) {
if (grid[i][j] == targetWord.charAt(0)) {
if (searchWordHelper(grid, targetWord, i, j, 0)) {
return true;
}
}
}
}
return false;
}

private static boolean searchWordHelper(char[][] grid, String targetWord, int row, int col, int index) {
if (index == targetWord.length()) {
return true;
}

if (row < 0 || row >= grid.length || col < 0 || col >= grid[0].length) {
return false;
}

if (grid[row][col] != targetWord.charAt(index)) {
return false;
}

char temp = grid[row][col];
grid[row][col] = '#';

boolean found = searchWordHelper(grid, targetWord, row + 1, col, index + 1) ||
searchWordHelper(grid, targetWord, row - 1, col, index + 1) ||
searchWordHelper(grid, targetWord, row, col + 1, index + 1) ||
searchWordHelper(grid, targetWord, row, col - 1, index + 1);

grid[row][col] = temp;

return found;
}
}

code antha correct kaadhu""konni inputs ki output wrong osthandhi


import java.util.*;

public class Main {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);

int n = scanner.nextInt();
int[] nums = new int[n];
for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
nums[i] = scanner.nextInt();
}

boolean canReachEnd = canJump(nums);
if (canReachEnd) {
System.out.println("True");
} else {
System.out.println("False");
}
}

private static boolean canJump(int[] nums) {
// Initialize an array to store the maximum reachable index from each position
int[] reachableIndices = new int[nums.length];
Arrays.fill(reachableIndices, -1);

// Starting from the last index, work backwards to determine the maximum reachable index from each position
reachableIndices[nums.length - 1] = nums.length - 1;
for (int i = nums.length - 2; i >= 0; i--) {
if (nums[i] == 0) {
continue; // Skip indices with a jump length of 0
}

int maxJump = nums[i];
for (int j = i + 1; j <= i + maxJump && j < nums.length; j++) {
reachableIndices[i] = Math.max(reachableIndices[i], reachableIndices[j]);
}
}

// Check if the first index can reach the last index
return reachableIndices[0] == nums.length - 1;
}
}

Counting Sort 1


import java.util.*;

public class Main {

public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);

int n = scanner.nextInt();
int[] arr = new int[n];

for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
arr[i] = scanner.nextInt();
}

// Sort the array in ascending order
Arrays.sort(arr);

// Find the minimum and maximum values in the array
int minValue = arr[0];
int maxValue = arr[n - 1];

// Count the frequency of each element
for (int i = minValue; i <= maxValue; i++) {
int count = 0;
for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
if (arr[j] == i) {
count++;
}
}
System.out.print(count + " ");
}
}
}

import java.io.*;
import java.util.*;
import java.text.*;
import java.math.*;
import java.util.regex.*;

public class Main {

public static int romanToDecimal(String romanNumber) {
int decimalNumber = 0;
int previousValue = 0;

for (int i = romanNumber.length() - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
int currentValue = romanToInt(romanNumber.charAt(i));

if (currentValue < previousValue) {
decimalNumber -= currentValue;
} else {
decimalNumber += currentValue;
}

previousValue = currentValue;
}

return decimalNumber;
}

private static int romanToInt(char romanChar) {
switch (romanChar) {
case 'I':
return 1;
case 'V':
return 5;
case 'X':
return 10;
case 'L':
return 50;
case 'C':
return 100;
case 'D':
return 500;
case 'M':
return 1000;
default:
return 0;
}
}

public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
String romanNumber = sc.nextLine();
int decimalNumber = romanToDecimal(romanNumber);

System.out.println(decimalNumber);
}
}

q-2





import java.io.*;
import java.util.*;
import java.text.*;
import java.math.*;
import java.util.regex.*;

import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.Scanner;

public class Main {

public static ArrayList<String> generateBrackets(int n) {
ArrayList<String> brackets = new ArrayList<>();
generateBrackets(n, 0, 0, new StringBuilder(), brackets);
return brackets;
}

private static void generateBrackets(int n, int open, int close, StringBuilder sb, ArrayList<String> brackets) {
if (open == n && close == n) {
brackets.add(sb.toString());
return;
}

if (open < n) {
sb.append('(');
generateBrackets(n, open + 1, close, sb, brackets);
sb.deleteCharAt(sb.length() - 1);
}

if (close < open) {
sb.append(')');
generateBrackets(n, open, close + 1, sb, brackets);
sb.deleteCharAt(sb.length() - 1);
}
}

public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
int n = scanner.nextInt();

ArrayList<String> brackets = generateBrackets(n);

brackets.forEach(System.out::print);
}
}

14/02/24, 10:38 - Deepu Vit Ecm: #include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <sys/wait.h>

int main() {
printf("Process A (Parent)\n");

// Creating process B
pid_t pidB = fork();

if (pidB == 0) {
// Code for process B
printf("Process B (Child of A)\n");

// Creating process D
pid_t pidD = fork();

if (pidD == 0) {
// Code for process D
printf("Process D (Child of B)\n");
exit(0); // Terminating process D
} else if (pidD > 0) {
// Code for process B to continue
wait(NULL); // Wait for process D to terminate
// Creating process E
pid_t pidE = fork();

if (pidE == 0) {
// Code for process E
printf("Process E (Child of B)\n");
exit(0); // Terminating process E
} else if (pidE > 0) {
wait(NULL); // Wait for process E to terminate
} else {
perror("Failed to fork E");
}
exit(0); // Terminating process B
} else {
perror("Failed to fork D");
}
} else if (pidB > 0) {
// Code for process A to continue
// Creating process C
pid_t pidC = fork();

if (pidC == 0) {
// Code for process C
printf("Process C (Child of A)\n");
exit(0); // Terminating process C
} else if (pidC > 0) {
wait(NULL); // Wait for process C to terminate
wait(NULL); // Wait for process B to terminate
} else {
perror("Failed to fork C");
}
} else {
perror("Failed to fork B");
}

return 0;
}

21/02/24, 16:47 - Snake(🐍): 1. Create process and print Parent ID and Child ID.

#include <sys/types.h>
#include <sys/wait.h>  // Include the sys/wait.h header
#include <stdio.h>
#include <unistd.h>

int main()
{
pid_t pid;

pid = fork();
if (pid < 0)
{
fprintf(stderr, "Fork Failed");
return 1;
}
else if (pid == 0)
{
printf("Child ID: %d\n", getpid());
execlp("/bin/ls", "ls", NULL);
}
else
{
wait(NULL);
printf("Parent ID: %d\n", getpid());
printf("Child Complete\n");
}
return 0;
}

2. Create orphan process program.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <sys/types.h>
#include <sys/wait.h>

int main() {
pid_t pid = fork();

if (pid == 0) {
// Child process
printf("Child process ID: %d\n", getpid());

// Create a new session and set the process group ID
if (setsid() == -1) {
printf("Error: setsid() failed\n");
return 1;
}

printf("Child process is now an orphan process\n");

// Do some work as an orphan process
sleep(10);

return 0;
} else if (pid > 0) {
// Parent process
printf("Parent process ID: %d\n", getpid());
printf("Child process ID: %d\n", pid);

// Wait for 1 second to allow the child process to become an orphan
sleep(1);

// Terminate the parent process
printf("Parent process is now terminating\n");
return 0;
} else {
// Error
printf("Error: fork() failed\n");
return 1;
}
}

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3. Write C program using wait() System call.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <sys/types.h>
#include <sys/wait.h>
#include <unistd.h>

void child_process() {
printf("In child process: PID=%d, PPID=%d\n", getpid(), getppid());
}

void parent_process() {
printf("In parent process: PID=%d\n", getpid());
int status;
pid_t pid = fork();

if (pid == 0) {
child_process();
} else if (pid > 0) {
wait(&status);  // wait for child process to finish
printf("Child process finished, status=%d\n", WEXITSTATUS(status));
} else {
printf("Fork failed\n");
}
}

int main() {
parent_process();
return 0;
}

4.. Create a process and compute factorial in child and Fibonacci in parent as executable.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <sys/types.h>
#include <unistd.h>

// Function to compute factorial
int factorial(int n) {
if (n == 0)
return 1;
else
return n * factorial(n - 1);
}

// Function to compute Fibonacci series
void fibonacci(int n) {
int t1 = 0, t2 = 1, nextTerm;
for (int i = 1; i <= n; ++i) {
printf("%d, ", t1);
nextTerm = t1 + t2;
t1 = t2;
t2 = nextTerm;
}
}

int main() {
pid_t pid = fork();  // create child process

if (pid == 0) {  // child process
printf("Child process:\n");
int num = 5;
printf("Factorial of %d is %d\n", num, factorial(num));
} else if (pid > 0) {  // parent process
printf("Parent process:\n");
int num = 10;
printf("Fibonacci series up to %d terms: ", num);
fibonacci(num);
printf("\n");
} else {
printf("Fork failed\n");
}

return 0;
}


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
5. Create a process and let child do some task like computing sum of N numbers.
#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <sys/types.h>
#include <signal.h>
#include <errno.h>

long long int sum_of_array(const int arr[], size_t n);

int main(int argc, char** argv) {
const int array[] = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5};
size_t length = sizeof(array) / sizeof(*array);

pid_t pid = fork();
if (pid < 0) {
perror("Error during fork");
exit(EXIT_FAILURE);
} else if (pid > 0) {
// Parent process
long long int result = sum_of_array(array, length);
printf("Sum computed by parent: %lld\n", result);
exit(EXIT_SUCCESS);
} else {
// Child process
long long int result = sum_of_array(array, length);
printf("Sum computed by child: %lld\n", result);
exit(EXIT_SUCCESS);
}
}

long long int sum_of_array(const int arr[], size_t n) {
long long int total = 0;
for (size_t i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
total += arr[i];
}
return total;
}



--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
6. Palindrome and ODD or EVEN as parent and child with fork.
#include <stdio.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

void isPalindrome(int number) {
int n, r, sum = 0, temp;
n = number;
temp = n;
while (n > 0) {
r = n % 10;
sum = (sum * 10) + r;
n = n / 10;
}
if (temp == sum)
printf("%d is a palindrome number\n", temp);
else
printf("%d is not a palindrome number\n", temp);
}

int main() {
int num;

printf("Enter a number: ");
scanf("%d", &num);

pid_t pid = fork();

if (pid < 0) {
fprintf(stderr, "Fork failed\n");
return 1;
} else if (pid == 0) {
// Child process
if (num % 2 == 0)
printf("%d is an even number\n", num);
else
printf("%d is an odd number\n", num);
} else {
// Parent process
isPalindrome(num);
}

return 0;
}

21/02/24, 19:58 - Somnath Reddy: #include<stdio.h>

void main() {
int i, NOP, sum=0, count=0, y, quant, wt=0, tat=0, bt[10], temp[10];
float avg_wt, avg_tat;

printf("Total number of processes in the system: ");
scanf("%d", &NOP);
y = NOP;

// Input burst times for processes
for(i = 0; i < NOP; i++) {
printf("\nEnter Burst time for Process[%d]: ", i+1);
scanf("%d", &bt[i]);
temp[i] = bt[i];
}

printf("\nEnter the Time Quantum for the process: ");
scanf("%d", &quant);

printf("\nGantt Chart:\n");
printf("-----------\n");
printf("0"); // Starting time

// Run the round robin algorithm
for(sum = 0, i = 0; y != 0; ) {
if(temp[i] <= quant && temp[i] > 0) {
sum = sum + temp[i];
printf("  P%d(%d-%d)", i+1, sum - temp[i], sum); // Print Gantt chart
temp[i] = 0;
count = 1;
}
else if(temp[i] > 0) {
printf("  P%d(%d-%d)", i+1, sum, sum + quant); // Print Gantt chart
temp[i] = temp[i] - quant;
sum = sum + quant;
}

if(temp[i] == 0 && count == 1) {
y--;
wt = wt + sum - bt[i];
tat = tat + sum;
count = 0;
}

if(i == NOP - 1) {
i = 0;
}
else if(i < NOP && bt[i + 1] > 0) {
i++;
}
else {
i = 0;
}
}

avg_wt = wt * 1.0 / NOP;
avg_tat = tat * 1.0 / NOP;

printf("\n-----------\n");

printf("\nAverage Turn Around Time: %f", avg_tat);
printf("\nAverage Waiting Time: %f\n", avg_wt);
}
